Objection of Grammatical Errors and Its Refutation
Presents and refutes the objection of grammatical errors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the typical objection that the Quran contains grammatical errors and the concise refutation that points to variant readings and grammatical licenses.

Core Idea
Alleged grammatical errors in the Quran are not errors but valid variant readings.

Critics have pointed to several Quranic verses that appear to violate standard Arabic grammar. In this passage, the author lists three such examples and then dismisses the claim by referring to the established science of Arabic syntax (i'rab), implying that these are known correct readings. This lesson examines the objection and its refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the full literal translation to understand the objection and refutation.
Notice the three examples cited.
2
Identify the three examples
Look at each example: 'inna hadhāni' (nominative after 'inna'), 'al-ṣābi'ūna' (nominative in a context requiring accusative), and 'al-muqīmīna' (accusative in a context requiring nominative). Understand why critics claim they are errors.
3
Understand the refutation
The refutation does not explain each case in detail but states that all such forms are correct as clarified in the science of grammar. This implies they follow valid qira'at or grammatical licenses.
The author trusts the reader to consult grammar sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها أن فيه خطأ الإعراب مثل : إنَّ هَذَانِ لَسَاحِرَانِ﴾ . وإنَّ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَالَّذِينَ هَادُوا والصَّابِئُونَ ) ولكنَّ الرَّاسِحُونَ في العلم منهم والمُؤْمِنُونَ يُؤْمِنُونَ بِمَا أُنْزِلَ إِلَيْكَ وَمَا أُنْزِلَ مِنْ قَبْلِكَ وَالْمُقِيمِينَ الصَّلاة . ورد بأن كل ذلك صواب على ما بين في علم الإعراب
And among them is that it contains grammatical errors such as: 'Indeed, these two are sorcerers' [Quran 20:63] and 'Indeed, those who have believed and those who were Jews and the Sabians' [Quran 2:62] and 'But those firm in knowledge among them and the believers believe in what has been revealed to you and what was revealed before you, and the ones who establish prayer' [Quran 4:162]. It is refuted by [saying] that all of that is correct as is explained in the science of grammar (i'rab).
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage presents the second objection: that the Quran contains grammatical errors (khat' al-i'rab). Three examples are cited: (1) 'inna hadhāni lasāhirān' where 'hadhāni' is nominative after 'inna' (which should be accusative), (2) 'wa-al-sābi'ūna' in a context where it should be accusative, and (3) 'wa-al-muqīmīna al-salāta' which appears accusative while grammatically it should be nominative. The refutation states that all these are correct according to certain valid qira'at (variant readings) or grammatical licenses that are explained in the science of Arabic syntax (ilm al-i'rab). The author does not elaborate further here, but directs to that science.

Key Terms
خطأ الإعراب
علم الإعراب
قراءات
إنَّ هَذَانِ لَسَاحِرَانِ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: People may think the Quran contains real grammatical errors due to apparent violations of standard rules.
Correction: These apparent errors are not errors but valid variant readings (qira'at) or grammatical licenses, as explained in the science of Arabic syntax.

Checkpoint
How does the author refute the claim of grammatical errors in the Quran?
A) By claiming the Quran is above grammar.
B) By stating that such forms are correct according to variant readings and grammatical principles.
C) By ignoring the objection.
D) By saying the Quran was revealed in a different dialect.

Key Takeaway
The Quran's apparent grammatical anomalies are resolved by variant readings and established grammatical rules, not errors.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a Quranic verse that seems grammatically odd at first glance, what is your immediate internal reaction? Do you doubt the revelation, or do you trust that there is a valid explanation and seek it? What does your response reveal about the strength of your faith in Allah's perfect speech?
?
Have you ever dismissed a claim against the Quran—whether grammatical or otherwise—without truly investigating it? What is one step you can take this week to learn a specific science (like qirā'āt or Arabic grammar) that equips you to respond to such objections with knowledge rather than blind belief?
?
The author of this passage points the reader to the science of grammar for resolution. Are you content to rely on scholars for every defense, or are you willing to study the tools needed to defend the Quran yourself? What concrete action will you take to move from passive acceptance to active understanding?
